## 1.2.182
- **Speed slider readout shows transition time (5%ŌåÆ95% in N min/hr) + Save popover viewport-clamp on mobile** ŌĆö small UX add and a mobile-clipping fix on `addon/rhythm-design.html`. **Speed readout (#36):** the wake/bed Speed sliders in the Sleep card previously showed `"6: crisp"` (level + label); now they show `"6: crisp ┬Ę ~3.5 hr"` ŌĆö the parenthetical is the time the logistic transition takes to walk from 5% to 95% of its range at that slope. Math: for a logistic with slope `k`, the 5%ŌåÆ95% width is `2 * ln(19) / k = 5.889 / k` hours. New helper `speedTransitionLabel(speedIdx)` reads `SPEED_TO_SLOPE[speedIdx]`, computes the width, and formats: under 60 minutes ŌåÆ `~N min` (rounded), under 10 hours ŌåÆ `~N.N hr` (1 decimal), else `~N hr` (rounded). New helper `formatSpeedReadout(speedIdx)` composes the full label string and is used in both `syncUIFromConfig` (to populate displays from a loaded config) and the two `updateSliderValue` formatter slots in `setupEventListeners` (so live drag updates the readout). Per-level transition times: Calm (0.4) ~14.7 hr, Gentle (0.6) ~9.8 hr, Soft (0.8) ~7.4 hr, Smooth (1.0) ~5.9 hr, Balanced (1.3) ~4.5 hr, Crisp (1.7) ~3.5 hr, Fast (2.3) ~2.6 hr, Snappy (3.0) ~2.0 hr, Quick (4.0) ~1.5 hr, Sharp (5.5) ~64 min, Flash (30.0) ~12 min, Instant (60.0) ~6 min ŌĆö gives users a concrete sense of "how slow is Calm really?" without staring at the chart. Scope kept to `rhythm-design.html` (the Sleep card on the redesigned page); not propagated to `area.html` / `areas.html` / `tune.html` since those pages weren't part of the round-4 polish thread ŌĆö easy to extend later if useful. **Save popover viewport-clamp (#37):** `.save-popover` is `position: absolute` inside `#chart-shell` with `transform: translateX(-50%)` to center on its `style.left` value (which is set to the wake/bed handle's `style.left` so the popover aims at the dragged pill). On mobile, when the wake handle sits near the left edge of the chart (e.g., wake at 10:45a in a chart anchored at 3a ŌåÆ handle ~32% across ŌåÆ close to viewport-left), the centered 240px-min popover overhangs the viewport's left edge and clips "SAVE WAKE" / "MoŌĆōFr" / etc. text. New: after `pop.classList.add('open')` (so dimensions are measurable), `getBoundingClientRect()` checks for left/right overshoot against `window.innerWidth` with an 8px margin and applies an additional `translateX(calc(-50% + Npx))` shift to nudge the popover back inside. Also resets the prior transform before measuring (so re-opening the popover after a previous clamp starts from a clean slate). Net behavior: popover now always lands fully inside the viewport on phones, regardless of which pill was tapped ŌĆö no clipped text. Net code: rhythm-design.html ~25 lines net (added: speedTransitionLabel + formatSpeedReadout helpers, popover clamp block; modified: 4 speed-readout call sites to use the new formatter).

## 1.2.181
- **Rhythm-zone graph polish round 4 ŌĆö Month chip moved to top-right (was overlapping "100%" y-axis label), popover title "Season" ŌåÆ "Month" (it's a month picker, not a season), Save popover header now reads the dragged-to time instead of the saved config value, "sun contribution" label flipped below the dotted curve (was getting blocked by the NOW pill), Month slider track fill bug fixed (was stuck at 50% regardless of handle position), type-in time entry on wake/bed/wake-alt/bed-alt displays for demo precision, new SUN DIMMING subsection in Brightness card mirroring Sun cooling pattern with its own toggle, chart sun-dim gate decoupled from Sun cooling (the toggle was incorrectly cross-wired), mobile CT label wrap onto two lines** ŌĆö nine coordinated polish changes on `addon/rhythm-design.html` (one bypass on `addon/primitives.py`), addressing user feedback after staring at v1.2.180 in production. **Month chip ŌåÆ top-right (#28):** v1.2.180 placed the chip at `top: 10px; left: 10px` which sat directly over the Plotly y-axis "100%" label, creating a stacked visual. Both `.month-chip` and `.month-popover` flipped to `right: 10px`; popover continues to drop down `top: 38px` from below the chip. **"Season" ŌåÆ "Month" (#29):** the popover title inside `#month-popover` read "Season" ŌĆö vestigial from an earlier seasonal-band concept ŌĆö but the slider stops at month boundaries (Jan, Feb, Mar...) and the chip label shows the month name, so the title was misleading. One-string swap. **Save popover header reads drag value (#30):** v1.2.178 introduced the working-copy decoupling pattern (drag updates `chartState.{wake,bed}DragVal` while `config.{wake,bed}_time` stays at the saved value until commit), but `openSavePopover()` at line 4307 still read `config.{wake,bed}_time` for the displayed time ŌĆö so dragging bed to 9:45p and clicking Save would show "Save bed to **9:00p**" (the old saved value) instead of "Save bed to **9:45p**" (what's about to be saved). Mirrors the same dragVal-or-config fallback pattern already used in `commitSave` and the curve renderer: `chartState.{wake,bed}DragVal != null ? dragVal : config.{wake,bed}_time`. **Sun-contribution label flipped below dotted line (#31):** v1.2.180's annotation used `yshift: 10` to float the "sun contribution" text 10px above the dotted reference curve at the point of maximum gap, but the dotted peak typically lands near the top of the chart (where bulb output is most depressed by sun) ŌĆö same vertical band where the NOW pill lives, so the pill's CCT-tinted background was partially or fully covering the label depending on cursor x. Flipped to `yshift: -10` so the label sits BELOW the dotted curve, in the gap region between bulb output and dotted reference ŌĆö semantically more correct too (the "sun contribution" IS the gap, so labeling INSIDE the gap reads as "this area is what the sun is contributing"). **Month slider track fill (#32):** the global `input[type=range]` CSS at line 358 paints the track with `linear-gradient(to right, var(--track-fill) var(--fill-pct, 50%), var(--track-empty) var(--fill-pct, 50%))` ŌĆö `--fill-pct` is updated per-slider by `updateSliderFill(el)` in response to `input` events. The month slider's input handler at line 5197 was missing the `updateSliderFill(monthSlider)` call, so the slider's track stayed stuck at the 50% default fall-through value regardless of where the handle was dragged ŌĆö visible as "fill stops at the middle of the track but the handle is at 70%" mismatch the user reported. Added one call in the input handler + one priming call after wiring (so the initial render gets the correct fill before any user interaction). **Type-in time entry on wake/bed displays (#33, the demo-precision feature):** the wake-time / bed-time / wake-alt-time / bed-alt-time sliders are 0.25-step (15-minute granularity) ŌĆö fine for everyday use but blocks demos where the user wants to land on a specific minute like "7:27a" to set up a transition that ends at a screencast-friendly moment. New `setupTimeInputEdit(displayId, sliderId)` makes the time-display span click-to-edit: tap ŌåÆ display swaps to a small text input prefilled with the current formatted time ŌåÆ user types `7:27a` (or `7:27am` or `7:27 AM` or `19:27` or `7` ŌåÆ assumed `7:00`) ŌåÆ Enter or blur commits, Escape reverts. New `parseTimeString(str)` utility handles all four formats via one regex `^(\d{1,2})(?::(\d{1,2}))?\s*(a|p|am|pm)?$` ŌĆö with `am`/`pm` it validates `1-12` hour range and applies the period; without, it validates `0-23` for 24-hour. On commit, the slider value is set (clamped to `[min, max]` and respecting the bed-slider's 0ŌĆō36 range so a typed `1:30a` after a current value past midnight pushes to `25.5` not `1.5`), the slider's existing `input` event fires (so the existing display/sync/render path runs), then `config.{wake,bed,wake_alt,bed_alt}_time` is overridden with the precise sub-step value (because slider step would otherwise round-trip the typed minutes back to the nearest quarter), `updateSliderFill` is called so the fill follows the new position, and `renderChart` re-runs. Mouse cursor on the display becomes `text` and a tooltip says "Click to type a precise time (e.g. 7:27a)" so the affordance is discoverable but unobtrusive. **SUN DIMMING subsection in Brightness card (#34):** v1.2.180's Brightness card had a single un-grouped "Sun response" row at the bottom (just label + reset + slider, no enable/disable, no surrounding container). Color card has a more deliberate pattern: two `.color-rule-stack` containers (Night warming, Sun cooling) each with a left-aligned bold label header + checkbox toggle + info icon, body collapses/greys when toggle is off. Brightness now mirrors this: wrapped the brightness-sensitivity row in `<div class="color-rule-stack" data-color-row="brightness-sensitivity">` with header label "Sun dimming" + new checkbox `#brightness-sensitivity-enabled` + info icon. New config key `brightness_sensitivity_enabled` (default `true`) added to defaults block, `BRIGHTNESS_FIELDS` allowlist, `syncConfigFromUI` (`config.brightness_sensitivity_enabled = checkbox.checked`), `syncUIFromConfig` (`checkbox.checked = config.brightness_sensitivity_enabled !== false`), the save-payload object in `saveZoneSettings`, and a new change listener on the checkbox that calls `syncColorRuleRows() + renderChart()`. `syncColorRuleRows()` extended to greys out `#brightness-sensitivity-body` when `brightness_sensitivity_enabled === false` (mirrors the existing `daylight-body` and `warm-night-body` greying pattern). **Chart sun-dim gate fix (bundled with #34):** the curve renderer at line 3414 used `config.daylight_enabled !== false` (Sun cooling toggle) to gate `showDottedTarget`, which meant turning Sun cooling on/off in the Color card was incorrectly toggling the brightness sun-dim curve in the chart ŌĆö the user spotted this immediately and called it out as the wrong coupling. Switched the gate to `config.brightness_sensitivity_enabled !== false` so the dotted reference curve and the visible bulb-output sun-dimming are now driven by the same flag the new SUN DIMMING checkbox controls. Backend symmetry: `addon/primitives.py:_get_natural_light_factor()` (line 688) now reads `zone_cfg.get("brightness_sensitivity_enabled", True)` and short-circuits to `return 1.0` when disabled, so unchecking the box bypasses the actual lighting calculation too ŌĆö not just the chart preview. Default `True` preserves the existing behavior for any zone configs that haven't seen the v1.2.181 UI yet. **Mobile CT label wrap (#35):** the Color gradient axis labels ("warmest", "coolest: night", "coolest: no-sun", "coolest: sunny") were single-line `white-space: nowrap` text, fine on desktop but at narrow phone-portrait widths with both Night warming + Sun cooling enabled (3+ "coolest:..." labels stacked horizontally) they overlap and cut off. New approach: rewrote the three "coolest:..." labels to use sub-spans ŌĆö `coolest<span class="ct-label-colon">: </span><span class="ct-label-sub">night</span>` ŌĆö so the same string renders as "coolest: night" on desktop. New `@media (max-width: 600px)` block flips `.ct-axis-ref .ct-axis-label` to `white-space: normal; line-height: 1.05; text-align: center` and switches `.ct-label-colon { display: none }` + `.ct-label-sub { display: block }` ŌĆö mobile reads as "coolest" (line 1) / "night" (line 2), no colon, both lines centered under the handle. Desktop unchanged ŌĆö sub-spans are inline by default. Net code: rhythm-design.html ~110 lines net (added: SUN DIMMING stack HTML + checkbox wiring + listener + body grey, parseTimeString + setupTimeInputEdit + 4 invocations, ct-axis-label sub-spans + media query; modified: chip CSS direction, popover title, openSavePopover dragVal, yshift sign, month slider fill calls, chart gate flag); primitives.py +3 (early-return short-circuit when `brightness_sensitivity_enabled` is False). config.yaml + build.yaml version bump to 1.2.181.

- **Rhythm-zone graph polish round 3 ŌĆö NOW pill Ōå║ becomes "Now" text, pillŌåÆx-axis connector trimmed flush + thicker default, conditions chip text-select hardened, "sun contribution" label on the dotted curve, bed-wrap UI bound (mirrors v1.2.128 workaround for the silent `% 24` shifted-midpoint wrap), Month moves from below-chart row to a tap-to-open chip in the chart top-left, Save+Reset chips combined into a single bordered container under the moved pill (Reset left, Save right), wake/bed pill drag now snaps to 15-minute ticks, today's day-letter underlined instead of marked with a stray under-dot, plus two new transition speeds (Flash k=30, Instant k=60) for live demos that sweep top-to-bottom in 4ŌĆō8 minutes** ŌĆö eleven coordinated changes on `addon/rhythm-design.html` (and brain.py / primitives.py / webserver.py / area.html / areas.html for the speed-table extension), addressing user feedback after staring at v1.2.179 in production. **NOW pill button (#17):** Ōå║ glyph replaced with the word "Now" ŌĆö clearer affordance, button widens to a small pill (`height: 18px; The renderChart loop tracks `maxGap` and `maxGapIdx` while building the gap-segmented arrays; on completion, if any gap > 0.75pp existed, push the annotation. The bulb curve stays unlabeled ŌĆö only the dotted reference needs naming, since "what bulbs output" is the chart's primary surface and reads cleanly without text. **Bed-wrap UI bound (#21):** the user reported "bedtime past midnight inverts the graph" ŌĆö confirmed the known `% 24` wrap on shifted midpoint described in the deferred audit memory note (`primitives.py:1187`-equivalent in rhythm-design.html's `calculateBrightnessAtHour:3151`). Math: bed=12:54a ŌåÆ bedFrame lifts to 24.9 in 48h frame ŌåÆ `computeShiftedMidpoint` shifts to Ōēł24.35 ŌåÆ silent `% 24` drops it to 0.35 ŌåÆ next clamp `Math.max(tDescend+0.01, ...)` slams 0.35 to 12.01 (= noon) ŌåÆ descent logistic midpoint at noon collapses brightness immediately. User chose path A: mirror the v1.2.128 UI-boundary workaround rather than do the deeper `% 24` cleanup (still deferred). New helper `computePhaseSignedOffset(kind)` returns the signed midpoint shift in hours (positive = later, negative = earlier) using the same brightness/slope math `computePhaseSafeOffset` already uses internally; `getPhaseBoundsInFrame` for kind=='bed' now adds `wrapHi = 24 - signedOff - 0.05` and applies `hi = Math.max(lo + 0.1, wrapHi)` if wrapHi tightens the existing hi. For brightness=25 + bed_speed=6: signedOff Ōēł -0.646 ŌåÆ wrapHi Ōēł 24.596 ŌåÆ max bed_time stops at Ōēł12:36a (acceptable workaround, user accepts the limitation in exchange for not chasing the silent wrap through the broader codebase). For brightness=50 (no shift), the bound is 23:57 (xA + 24 ŌłÆ 0.05 ŌåÆ wrapHour to 23.95) ŌĆö unchanged. **Month chip in solar band (#22):** v1.2.179 collapsed the Month row into a tap-to-expand reveal-group below the chart, but it still ate ~50px of vertical space below the plot and the Month/April flanking text felt out of place. New: removed the entire `.month-row` from below the chart; added a small `.month-chip` button at top-left of `#chart-shell` (mirroring the `live-fab` position on top-right) showing "­¤ōģ April"; click toggles a `.month-popover` that drops down with the existing slider (`min=0 max=11`). Document-level click-outside dismisses the popover. New: `setupHandleDrag.moveTo` rounds `tFrame` to the nearest 0.25h (`Math.round(tFrame * 4) / 4`) before clamping, matching the existing wake-time/bed-time slider step in the Sleep card (`step="0.25"`). Net feel: drag snaps to 15-minute ticks (12:00a, 12:15a, 12:30a, ...) so users land on exact times without precision pointing. **Today day-letter underline (#25):** v1.2.179 marked today with a 4px round dot positioned `bottom: -5px` BELOW the day-indicator circle. Visually this looked like a stray dot floating between rows ŌĆö the user said it read "as a circle below the second one." New: replaced with a 12├Ś1.5px accent-colored line positioned `bottom: 3px` INSIDE the day-indicator circle (under the letter, like an underline). When the day is also `.active` (filled white background), the underline switches to black for contrast (`.day-indicator.today.active::after { background: #000 }`). Reads as a true "today" mark on the letter itself rather than a stray bullet underneath. **Speed levels 11 + 12 (#26):** user wanted to demo a top-to-bottom transition in 3-5 minutes for someone ŌĆö the existing max (Sharp, k=5.5) takes ~44 minutes for a 90% logistic transition, way too slow for a live demo. Two new levels appended to the speed table: **11 = "Flash" (k=30)** completes 90% transition in ~8 minutes, **12 = "Instant" (k=60)** in ~4 minutes. Source-of-truth `SPEED_TO_SLOPE` in `addon/brain.py:66` extended `[..., 5.5, 30.0, 60.0]`; mirrors in `addon/area.html:1537`, `addon/areas.html:1235`, `addon/rhythm-design.html:2067` extended identically. `SPEED_LABELS` array in rhythm-design.html extended `[..., 'Sharp', 'Flash', 'Instant']`. Wake/bed speed slider `max="10"` ŌåÆ `max="12"` in rhythm-design.html (line 1808, 1874). All 28 `Math.min(10, ŌĆ”)` / `min(10, ŌĆ”)` clamps across brain.py, primitives.py, webserver.py, area.html, areas.html, rhythm-design.html bumped to 12 ŌĆö sed-style bulk replace, verified zero remaining. The new levels are intentionally aggressive (kAscend=60 means the logistic transitions through 90% of its range in under 4 minutes) ŌĆö they're not for daily use, they're for showing a viewer "watch the lights walk from cool to warm in real time." Picking Flash/Instant for the wake or bed speed in the Sleep card and then using the chart cursor or the `step_up`/`step_down` primitives at the demo time will produce visible bulb-color shifts every few seconds. ## 1.2.179
- **Rhythm-zone graph polish round 2 ŌĆö solid white cursor line, swapped curves so the visible solid is the actual bulb output (sun-dimmed) and the dotted reference is the un-dimmed room target ONLY in the gap region, separate colored hover/drag cursor on wake/bed pills (white cursor stays put), reset button moved INTO the NOW pill (standalone Now button removed), conditions chip restyled to plain "ŌśĆ 80%" matching sunrise/sunset, and Month collapsed into a tap-to-expand row matching the Brightness/Speed pattern** ŌĆö third iteration on the redesigned `addon/rhythm-design.html`, addressing six pieces of user feedback in one ship after staring at the v1.2.178 result. **Solid cursor line:** `cursorLineStyle` in `applyCursor()` dropped `dash: 'dot'` ŌĆö was reading as a flicker against the gridlines, now reads as a clean unambiguous time marker. **Curves swapped + dotted clipped to gap region (the big one):** v1.2.178's visible solid line plotted `brightnessPct` (the room TARGET ŌĆö what brightness the area should be at, ignoring sun) and the dotted line plotted `brightnessPct ├Ś sunDimFactor` (the actual bulb output after sun-dim is subtracted). User said this was backwards: "main curve should be the one for light bulb output, the dotted line should be the sun-enriched portion." The reframing makes the chart honest: the visible solid is what the bulb will physically emit, the dotted shows what brightness the bulb is *being relieved of* by the sun. Implementation: introduced `roomTargetPct = brightness ├Ś 100` (un-dimmed) and `brightnessPct = roomTargetPct ├Ś sunDimFactor(hours[i])` (the new visible curve). The CCT-tinted fill+line loop and the hover trace now plot `brightnessPct` (sun-dimmed). The dotted reference now plots `roomTargetPct` SEGMENTED ŌĆö a 0.75pp gap-threshold filter (`if roomTargetPct[i] - brightnessPct[i] > 0.75`) builds a sparse `dx`/`dy` array with `null` separators, so the dotted line only appears in the regions where the curves actually diverge (typically mid-day when sun is lifting bulb output below room target). `connectgaps: false` on the trace tells Plotly to honor the breaks. Net effect: at night both curves coincide ŌåÆ no dotted line at all; at noon with full sun ŌåÆ dotted appears above the solid showing the sun-contribution gap; at dawn/dusk ŌåÆ dotted appears in the partial-overlap zones. **Cursor pill + hover trace updated to bulb output:** `cursorPoint.y` in `applyCursor()` now reads `calculateBrightnessAtHour ├Ś sunDimFactor`, so the white cursor circle sits ON the visible solid curve (not floating above it where the un-dimmed value used to be). NOW pill text `${bri}%` shows bulb output too, matching what the user sees on the curve. Hover trace `hoverDetails` text already reads from `brightnessPct` so it picked up the sun-dimming for free. `chartState.sunDimFactor` exposed from `renderChart` so `applyCursor` and `positionOverlays` use the same factor without duplicating the elevation/condition math. **Pill hover/drag spawns separate colored cursor (the second big one):** v1.2.178's `pointerenter` on a pill saved `cursorHour` and replaced it with the pill's time, then called `applyCursor()` ŌĆö visually this MOVED the white cursor over to the pill, which the user found confusing ("the cursor line and pill jump over to that; it should stay put"). New behavior: hover/drag spawns a SECOND cursor ŌĆö a phase-colored vertical line (blue `ASCEND_COLORS.text` for wake, yellow `DESCEND_COLORS.text` for bed) plus a CCT-tinted circle on the visible bulb-output curve at the pill's x. The white time-cursor stays exactly where it was. Implementation: added `chartState.wakeHovering`/`bedHovering` flags; `setupHandleDrag`'s `pointerenter`/`pointerleave` set the flag and call `renderChart()` (no more cursorHour stomping, no more `applyCursor()` calls). The renderChart drag-circle + drag-line code already existed for `wakeDragActive`/`bedDragActive` but only fired during active drag ŌĆö generalized the trigger to `wakeShown = wakeDragActive || wakeHovering` so the same colored cursor appears on hover too. Marker `line.color` swapped from `rgba(0,0,0,0.55)` to the phase tint so the circle's outline matches its vertical line. Pill colored cursor disappears the moment pointer leaves or drag releases. Net UX: user can hover wake at 6:45a ŌåÆ blue cursor appears showing "if I save here, this is what bulb output will be," white time-cursor stays at noon (or wherever it was). Drag-and-release ŌåÆ blue cursor follows the pill, vanishes on release if no other interaction. **Reset (Ōå║) moved INTO the NOW pill, standalone Now button removed:** v1.2.178's "Now" button was a centered chip below the chart that snapped cursor back to current time ŌĆö visually it floated in no-man's-land between chart and Month row, and the user said it should live with the cursor pill since the pill IS the cursor control. New: when `cursorTrackingNow === false` (cursor has been scrubbed away from now), the NOW pill innerHTML appends ` <button class="now-pill-reset" title="Jump to current time">Ōå║</button>`; click jumps cursor back to current time and re-flips `cursorTrackingNow = true` (which makes the periodic auto-advance loop pick it back up). When tracking is on, the button isn't rendered ŌĆö pill just shows time/bri/cct as before, no clutter. CSS: `.now-pill` switched to `display: inline-flex` so the button can sit inline with the readout text, `pointer-events: auto` on `.now-pill-reset` (the pill itself stays `pointer-events: none` so dragging on the chart works through it), 18├Ś18 round button with `rgba(0,0,0,0.18)` background that adapts to whatever CCT-tint the pill has at that moment. Removed: `<div class="chart-below-row"><button class="time-nav-btn" id="cursor-time-now">Now</button></div>` HTML, `.chart-below-row` and `.time-nav-btn` CSS rules (~37 lines). Click handler delegated on `#now-pill` so it doesn't need rebinding on each render. **Conditions chip restyled to plain text matching sunrise/sunset:** v1.2.178 had the conditions chip as a pill (background, border, padding, larger font) and the icon switched between sun/partly/cloudy/storm/fog/dark based on percent. User feedback: make it visually consistent with the sunrise/sunset labels (which are plain 10px text in the same solar band) ŌĆö drop the pill background, always show a sun ŌśĆ icon (the percent already conveys cloudiness, the icon-switching was redundant info), match the font size/color/weight exactly. Implementation: `.outdoor-chip` CSS background ŌåÆ transparent, border ŌåÆ none, padding ŌåÆ 0, font-size 11px ŌåÆ 10px, color ŌåÆ `rgba(215,215,215,0.75)` (matches `.solar-label`), `bottom: 60px` ŌåÆ `65px` (aligns vertically with sunrise/sunset). `.outdoor-chip:hover` color brightens to `rgba(255,255,255,0.95)` (mirroring `.solar-label:hover`). `updateChipIcon()` simplified ŌĆö `iconEl.textContent = '\u2600'` (always sun), no more pct-based icon selection. Click still toggles the popover via the existing handler ŌĆö interaction unchanged, just the visual presentation. Reads as "sunrise / ŌśĆ 80% / sunset" ŌĆö three peer labels in the same band, the conditions one happens to be tappable. **Month collapsed to tap-to-expand row:** v1.2.178's month row was a label + slider always visible, taking ~50px of vertical real estate even when not being adjusted. User asked to match the Brightness/Speed pattern below ŌĆö collapsed shows just the row, tap expands the slider in a smooth reveal. Implementation: wrapped `.month-row` with `class="month-row reveal-group"` and restructured contents to use `.tune-control-row` + `.tune-slider-row` (the same DOM/CSS pattern wake-time/bed-time/brightness/speed already use). The existing `initAutoHideSliders()` global click handler picks up the new `.reveal-group` for free ŌĆö no JS changes needed. Removed the custom `.month-row` flex layout + `.month-label` `min-width: 80px` styling and the bespoke `.month-slider` thumb CSS (now inherits the standard tune-slider style for consistency). New CSS: `.month-row { padding-top: 6px }` + `.month-row > .tune-slider-row { padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 14px }` (slider full-width when revealed). Net: collapsed state now reads "Month  April" left-aligned at the same indent as Brightness/Speed below; tap anywhere on the row ŌåÆ slider drops down ŌåÆ drag changes month ŌåÆ tap elsewhere collapses. **Net code:** rhythm-design.html ~80 lines net (added: separate-cursor logic, gap-threshold dotted segmenter, reset button styling, restructured month row; removed: chart-below-row HTML+CSS, custom month-row CSS, hover-cursor stomping logic). No backend changes ŌĆö webserver.py untouched.

## 1.2.178
- **Rhythm-zone graph polish pass ŌĆö phase-bound clamps on wake/bed handles (mirrored from area-details), x-axis anchored at the real `cfg.ascend_start` (not derived), drag decoupled from the Sleep accordion (preview-until-Save), sun-dim dotted reference line that actually shows the sun's effect, hover-preview on pills, pillŌåÆx-axis connector lines, text-select fix on solar labels, AND a 60s heartbeat watchdog for Live Design that ends abandoned sessions** ŌĆö second iteration on v1.2.177's `rhythm-design.html` redesign, addressing eight pieces of user feedback in one ship. **Phase bounds (correctness):** ported `computePhaseSafeOffset` + the new `getPhaseBoundsInFrame` helper from `area.html:3083` into rhythm-design ŌĆö wake clamps to `[ascend_start + safeOffset, descend_start ŌłÆ safeOffset]` and bed to `[descend_start + safeOffset, (ascend_start+24) ŌłÆ safeOffset]`, with the safe-offset narrowed by brightness-shifted-midpoint math (`SPEED_TO_SLOPE[wake_speed]` + `wake_brightness%` ŌåÆ log-term offset) so the inverted-midpoint can never escape the phase. Plus a 4-hour minimum-sleep-window guard between bed and wake. Falls back to a permissive ┬▒0.05h band if the brightness/slope combo would invert the bounds (matches area.html's safety net). Replaces the temporary `xA + 0.25 / bedT ŌłÆ 6h` clamps that allowed wake/bed to cross phase boundaries. **X-axis anchor (correctness):** `recomputeAscendStart()` now reads `config.ascend_start` directly (typically 3a for adult, 0a for young child, 8a for nightowl, etc., per the existing sleep-pattern presets at lines 2053ŌĆō2058) instead of the v1.2.177 mock-derived `wrapHour(config.wake_time ŌłÆ 2)`. Fixes the user's "x-axis starts at 5a but the phase starts at 3a" complaint ŌĆö chart now lines up with the actual ascend boundary regardless of wake time, matching `area.html:2226`'s `xAnchor = cfg.ascend_start` pattern. **Drag decoupled from Sleep accordion (UX):** v1.2.177 dragged a wake/bed pill and `config.wake_time` updated immediately, which mutated the Sleep accordion below the chart in real-time ŌĆö the user said "feels wrong, the chip's existence already signals unsaved." Drag now writes only to `chartState.wakeDragVal` / `bedDragVal` (the working copy that already existed but was being mirrored to config); curve and handle position read `dragVal ?? config.wake_time`, so the chart previews live but the Sleep accordion stays at the saved value until commit. `commitSave()` reads from `dragVal` (not config) to get the value to persist. `resetWakeOrBed()` simplified to just clearing `dragVal` (no config rollback needed since config was never touched). `resolveEffectiveTiming()` and `positionOverlays()` updated to check `dragVal != null` (not `dragActive`) so the preview persists between drag-release and Save/Reset. **Sun-dim dotted line (was invisible, now meaningful):** v1.2.177's "sun-contribution dotted reference" plotted `targetBri = brightnessPct` ŌĆö i.e. the SAME curve as the bulb-output line, so it was literally invisible (line on top of line). New formula computes `sunDimFactor(h) = max(0, 1 ŌłÆ elevationToOutdoorNorm(elev, conditionMult) ├Ś brightness_sensitivity)` and plots `targetBri[i] = brightnessPct[i] ├Ś sunDimFactor(hours[i])`, which produces a dotted reference that sits BELOW the bulb-output curve during daylight (more sun ŌåÆ bigger gap, showing how much the bulbs are dimming to compensate). Driven by all three signals the user requested: month slider (sun elevation varies by date-of-year), outdoor chip value (`conditionMult` = current sensor or manual pick), and `config.brightness_sensitivity` (the per-zone "sun response" knob). Reuses the existing `getSunElevationAtHour()` and `elevationToOutdoorNorm()` from rhythm-design's already-loaded sun helpers ŌĆö no new astronomy code. Only renders if max gap > 0.5pp so it stays out of the way at night or when sensitivity is zero. **Hover preview on pills (UX):** `pointerenter` on the wake/bed pill now temporarily moves `cursorHour` to the pill's time and calls `applyCursor()`, so the dotted vertical line + CCT-tinted circle on the curve + NOW pill above the curve all preview the bulb values that wake/bed will produce ŌĆö without the user having to grab the pill. `pointerleave` restores the saved cursor position. Skipped on touch (`e.pointerType === 'touch'`) and during active drag to avoid stomping the real interaction. Saves the user from having to drag-and-release-and-undo just to peek at "what would brightness be at 9:30am?" **PillŌåÆx-axis connector (UX):** thin 1px CSS pseudo-element on `.phase-handle::before` extends 56px above the pill, phase-tinted (`#5cb3ff` for wake, `#ffe680` for bed), opacity 0.25 default ŌåÆ 0.55 on hover or active drag. Visually anchors the pill to the chart so the eye doesn't have to track horizontally ŌĆö wake pill clearly points to its column on the curve. **Text-select fix:** added `user-select: none; -webkit-user-select: none` to `.solar-label` ŌĆö sunrise/sunset labels were getting selected during pill drags (they sit in the same y-band the pointer travels through), looking like sloppy mouse-drag selection. **Live Design heartbeat watchdog (server + client, the abandoned-browser fix):** the user noticed SunOffice (test_1) was missing from the periodic update loop ŌĆö root cause was an old browser tab still holding it as the active Live Design area, which the periodic loop deliberately skips (`main.py:6256`). New solution: browser pings `POST /api/live-design/heartbeat` every 30s while a Live Design session is active for the selected area; server tracks `live_design_started_at` + `live_design_last_heartbeat` (added to `LightDesignerServer.__init__`); a background `_live_design_watcher()` task launched in `start_serving()` polls every 15s and, if no heartbeat has arrived for 60s (`LIVE_DESIGN_TIMEOUT_SEC`), ends the Live Design session ŌĆö calls `state.set_is_circadian(area_id, True)` to put the area back under Circadian control + `client.handle_live_design(area_id, False)` to release the lock + clears the in-memory cache. Doesn't restore saved light states (the manual-end path does that for explicit Stop clicks); the watcher's job is just to free the area for periodic updates, lights resume circadian on the next 20s tick. Heartbeat endpoint is no-op if `area_id` doesn't match the active session (so a stale browser holding `test_1` can't keep an active `kitchen` session alive). Client side: `startLiveDesignHeartbeat(areaId)` + `stopLiveDesignHeartbeat()` helpers wired into the four Live Design lifecycle paths in rhythm-design.html ŌĆö area-select start, Stop button, area-change-to-null, and the page-unload `stopLiveDesign()` cleanup. Net effect on the bug the user reported: even if a browser tab is closed without a clean Stop, the server reclaims the area within ~75s (60s threshold + up to 15s watcher interval) ŌĆö no more "test_1 mysteriously frozen out of periodic updates." Heartbeat is cheap (one POST per 30s) and the cache-warm cost is the user's already-open tab. **Net code:** rhythm-design.html grows by the new helpers + heartbeat client (~70 lines net); webserver.py adds the heartbeat endpoint, the watcher task, and the start/end-of-session timestamp updates (~80 lines net). All existing Live Design flows preserved ŌĆö heartbeat is purely additive.

## 1.2.177
- **Rhythm-zone graph redesign ŌĆö direct-manipulation light-design tool with x=0 anchored at ascend_start (no phase wrap), draggable cursor + draggable wake/bed pill handles, NOW pill above curve, outdoor-conditions chip in solar band, month slider, save popover scoped to weekday/weekend/all-days** ŌĆö large redesign of the primary light-design surface in `addon/rhythm-design.html` (the page where the user models their home's circadian rhythm, where dozens of hours of tuning happen). Replaces the old chart's day-of-year slider + variant checkboxes + below-chart cursor callout + dropdown-style outdoor selector with the area-details direct-manipulation pattern: the cursor is a draggable dot on the curve (tap-to-jump or drag-to-scrub), wake and bed are draggable pill-shaped handles in the bottom margin (full blue/yellow background with dark text ŌĆö `--wake: #5cb3ff`, `--bed: #ffe680`), the NOW pill sits above the curve at cursor x with CCT-tinted background matching the bulb output at that time, and sunrise/sunset/outdoor-conditions all sit in a single "solar band" below the chart with vertically-aligned centers (chip is taller than the words, so different `bottom` values matched at center). Sunrise/sunset are now HTML overlays with crisp `:hover::after` tooltips instead of Plotly annotations. Sun-contribution dotted reference line drawn when `outdoor > 0 AND sun_response > 0` to show the curve's "target" before sun fill is subtracted. **Anchored x-axis (the structural change):** chart x-range is now `[ascendStart, ascendStart + 24]` instead of `[0, 24]`, with `ascendStart = config.ascend_start` (typically a few hours before wake). Means bed never wraps to the left edge even when pushed past midnight ŌĆö the whole sleep phase reads left-to-right as one contiguous span. Curve generation lifts wake/bed into the same 48h frame; `visHour(h, xAnchor)` maps stored 0ŌĆō24 hours into the visible frame; `pxToHour` wraps back when storing. Re-anchors only on save (not mid-drag) so chart doesn't slide under the user's finger. Pattern adopted from `area.html:2226` (`xAnchor = cfg.ascend_start; xEnd = xAnchor + 24`). **Schedule grouping (UX simplification):** the 4-combo wake├Śbed variant model (wake1+bed2, wake2+bed1) was simplified to today's-schedule-only ŌĆö chart shows whichever wake/bed pair applies to today based on `config.wake_alt_days` / `bed_alt_days`. Save popover after dragging a pill offers three scopes: existing-group-containing-today (left blue border to mark "today's group"), other existing group, and "All days" (sets primary, clears alt arrays). No "Custom" option ŌĆö granular day editing belongs in the Sleep accordion (which is preserved unchanged below the chart). On commit, calls existing `saveZoneSettings()` so persistence flow is identical to before ŌĆö only the surface changed. **Outdoor conditions chip** replaces the old `<select id="modeled-conditions">` dropdown but reuses the same backend storage (`_liveConditionMult`); popover has Current (default ŌĆö reads sensor) and Pick value (Sunny / Partly cloudy / Cloudy / Stormy / Fog / Dark) tabs. Current is intentionally the default so the chart drops the user into "live state of their home" ŌĆö known anchor for forward/back scrubbing ŌĆö rather than an arbitrary modeled value. **Month slider replaces day-of-year slider** (12 stops vs 365 ŌĆö much faster to drag, and the math difference between "April 8" and "April 22" isn't meaningful for a yearly-rhythm view). Slider position drives sunrise/sunset, which drives the sun-contribution dotted line, which drives the bulb-output curve via the existing `adjustCCTForSolarRules`. Month name displayed live as user drags. **Phase bounds restored on the new pill handles:** wake clamps to `[xAnchor + 0.25, bedT ŌłÆ 6h]`, bed clamps to `[wakeT + 6h, xAnchor + 24 ŌłÆ 0.25]` ŌĆö wake can never cross bed minus a 6h sleep window, and bed can never reach the wrap boundary at the right edge of the chart (so the no-wrap invariant is enforced at the input layer, not just visually). **Cursor and wake/bed drag-circles are CCT-tinted** (color of the bulb at that time) rather than phase-colored, keeping the curve color-honest; phase color stays on the pill in the bottom margin where it identifies the handle. Ghost pill at the saved position appears only during active drag, not after release ŌĆö Reset chip is the recovery path once the user has let go. Save and Reset chips sit BELOW the moved pill (not above) so they don't clobber the solar band. Save chip is white (matches Reset), not green ŌĆö green reads like "valid form" / success-state, and the chip's existence already signals "unsaved change." **Removed:** `#chart-date-slider` + `#chart-date-display` (replaced by month slider), `#chart-schedule-toggles` and the `#chart-wake-secondary`/`#chart-bed-secondary` checkboxes (variant viewing dropped ŌĆö chart shows today only), `#cursor-callout` (replaced by NOW pill above the curve), `#modeled-conditions` dropdown (replaced by outdoor chip popover, backend storage unchanged), four time-nudge buttons `cursor-time-minus-30`/`-5`/`+5`/`+30` (replaced by cursor drag ŌĆö the **Now** button is preserved as a one-tap "jump to live time"). Plotly sunrise/sunset annotations + dotted vertical guides also removed (replaced by HTML overlays). **Bug fix as a side benefit:** `margin.l` bumped 36 ŌåÆ 50, fixing a long-standing y-axis "100%" label clip ("00%" was visible). **Existing wiring preserved unchanged:** `saveZoneSettings()`, `resolveEffectiveTiming()`, `applyLiveLight()`, the Sleep / CT / Brightness accordions, live-design controls (FAB + area selection), the `_liveConditionMult` cache, `getValuesAtTime()` / `cctToRGB()` / `adjustCCTForSolarRules()`. The new UI is a different surface for these, not a replacement. **Behavior change worth flagging:** `commitSave` auto-persists via `saveZoneSettings()` on every wake/bed save-popover commit (the chip-popover-commit IS the save action). Old flow required hitting a separate section-level Save button. This matches the locked design spec but is a behavior delta from the old chart ŌĆö no draft-only mode. Net: 6,125 lines (up from 5,927; +198 net = 1,127 inserts, 519 deletes). Mock at `addon/rhythm-design-mock.html` is the spec / source of truth and is included in the commit for design provenance.

## 1.2.176
- **Drop the in-nav DEV/BETA pill ŌĆö keep the `[DEV]`/`[BETA]` document-title prefix only** ŌĆö v1.2.174 added an outlined orange/blue pill into the addon nav next to the brand link, plus the title prefix, plus the per-branch corner-stamped icon (D/B). On mobile the pill pushes "Settings" off the right edge of the nav (last two letters get cut off), and it's redundant with the corner-stamped icon that already sits in the same header. The icon-in-nav + tab-title-prefix combo is enough to differentiate channels at a glance without consuming nav space. `initChannelBadge()` (`shared.js`) trimmed to just the title-prefix branch ŌĆö fetch `/api/channel`, early-return on `main` or fetch failure, prepend `[DEV]` / `[BETA]` to `document.title` if not already present. Removed: the `.channel-badge` CSS injection, the `.nav-brand` DOM insertion, and the dev/beta color constants. Endpoint, `addon/.channel` plumbing, and Dockerfile COPY all unchanged. Function name kept as `initChannelBadge` for now even though it no longer injects a badge ŌĆö the `init*` pattern matches sibling startup helpers and renaming would touch the DOMContentLoaded listener for no UX gain.

## 1.2.175
- **Fix: in-UI channel badge missing on dev/beta ŌĆö `addon/.channel` wasn't being copied into the container image** ŌĆö v1.2.174 shipped the channel-identity plumbing (`addon/.channel` per branch + `/api/channel` endpoint + `initChannelBadge()` injection of the orange/blue outlined pill into the nav and `[DEV]`/`[BETA]` document title prefix), and the corner-stamped icon/logo + repository.yaml name suffix were correctly differentiating in HA's repo list and supervisor list. But on the dev addon at runtime, the orange "DEV" pill never appeared in the UI and `[DEV]` never prefixed the tab title ŌĆö even though v1.2.174 was confirmed installed and the D-stamped icon next to "Home" was visible. Network tab showed `/api/channel` returning `{"channel": "main"}` despite `addon/.channel` containing `dev` on the dev branch in git. Root cause: `addon/Dockerfile:19` copies the addon source into the image with the glob `COPY *.py *.html *.js *.png requirements.txt ./` ŌĆö that pattern excludes dotfiles like `.channel` (and would also exclude a non-dotfile `channel` since it has no extension matching the glob list). The file existed in the repo but never made it into the running container, so `_get_channel()` (`webserver.py:_get_channel`) hit its file-not-found branch and returned the fallback "main"; `initChannelBadge()` then took the early-return path for `channel === 'main'` and rendered nothing. The static icon worked because `*.png` in the existing glob already matched `icon.png`/`logo.png`. Fix: add an explicit second COPY directive `COPY .channel ./` immediately after the existing COPY line. Kept the dotfile name (it's metadata, conventional). One-line Dockerfile change, no Python or JS edit needed; v1.2.175 build will rebuild the image with the file present, `_get_channel()` will read `dev`/`beta`/`main` correctly per branch, and the badge + title prefix will render. Also a useful precedent: dotfiles in `addon/` need explicit COPY directives ŌĆö the existing glob pattern won't pick them up, and silently falling back to a default value (as `_get_channel()` does) makes the breakage invisible until you check the network tab. (The same gotcha bit `_get_addon_version()` in v1.2.172, which is why that version had to switch to reading from a build-arg ENV instead of `config.yaml` ŌĆö but `.channel` is per-branch and we don't want it in build.yaml, so the explicit COPY is the right fix here.)

## 1.2.174
- **Channel identity per branch: distinct repo name + addon icon/logo on dev/beta/main + in-UI channel badge** ŌĆö addresses the user's "I can't tell dev from beta from main when both are installed in HA" pain. Two layers of differentiation now ship together. **Layer 1 ŌĆö channel files in git:** dev/beta/main each carry a different `repository.yaml` `name` ("Circadian Light by HomeGlo (Dev)" / "(Beta)" / unsuffixed for stable), a different `addon/icon.png` and `addon/logo.png` (corner-stamped "D" or "B" badge generated via Pillow from the original logo, white circle with navy letter overlapping the gradient ring; stable keeps the original unbadged), and a new `addon/.channel` text file containing `dev` / `beta` / `main`. Color-only differentiation rejected because (a) HA sidebar's `panel_icon` is MDI (always monochrome) and (b) HA desaturates the addon logo to grayscale when the addon is stopped ŌĆö corner letter stamp survives both. Per-branch identity protected via `.gitattributes merge=ours` on the four files (repository.yaml, addon/icon.png, addon/logo.png, addon/.channel) so future dev ŌåÆ beta ŌåÆ main merges propagate code and version normally but never overwrite identity. Requires `git config merge.ours.driver true` once per clone (built-in `ours` driver isn't registered by default); new `scripts/setup-git.sh` one-liner does this and is documented for fresh-clone onboarding. **Layer 2 ŌĆö in-UI channel badge:** new `/api/channel` endpoint reads `addon/.channel` once at startup and exposes the value; `shared.js` fetches on every page load and, for dev or beta only, injects an outlined pill ("DEV" in `#feac60` orange / "BETA" in `#5fa8ff` blue) into the nav next to the brand link, plus prefixes the document title with `[DEV]` / `[BETA]` so the browser tab differentiates too. Outlined-pill style chosen over solid-fill because it's visible at a glance but doesn't compete with content; main shows nothing (stable should look "normal"). Badge code is one self-contained function `initChannelBadge()` that gracefully no-ops if the API fetch fails (running outside HA, network error, etc.). The plumbing avoids touching `addon/config.yaml` (which propagates version through merges and would force a partial-merge gymnastic) by routing identity through `addon/.channel` instead ŌĆö clean separation between "what the addon IS" (per-branch) and "what version it's at" (cross-branch).

## 1.2.173
- **Person trigger category now matches `_person` (in addition to `_person_detected`/`_human_detected`/`_human`) ŌĆö Reolink Duo 3 WiFi's `binary_sensor.*_person` entity was leaking into "show all" instead of the Person row** ŌĆö `TRIGGER_CATEGORIES.presence` (`control.html:2008`) defines keywords each category checks against entity_ids to decide what shows in the categorized Presence/Event rows vs the uncategorized "show all" expander. Pet had `_animal` (bare), Vehicle had `_vehicle` (bare), but Person only had `_person_detected`, `_human_detected`, `_human` ŌĆö missing `_person` (bare). Reolink (and likely some other camera/motion brands) report the bare suffix without `_detected`. Net effect: a fresh Reolink had its motion entity correctly under "Any motion", animal under "Pet", vehicle under "Vehicle", but person fell through to "show all" ŌĆö visually inconsistent and confusing for the user since the other three categorize cleanly. Fix: add `_person` to the Person keyword list. One-line keyword array edit; no logic change. Curation note for future allowlist adds (caught while triaging this report): when adding a new model to MOTION_SENSOR_MODELS / CAMERA_MODELS / CONTACT_SENSOR_MODELS, audit each `trigger_patterns` entry against `TRIGGER_CATEGORIES` keyword lists ŌĆö anything that doesn't match will leak to "show all". This step would have caught the `_person` gap when v1.2.172 added the Reolink Duo 3 WiFi entry.

## 1.2.172
- **Reolink Duo 3 WiFi added to CAMERA_MODELS allowlist + report payload now sends model and model_id separately + addon_version no longer "unknown" in reports + build.yaml ADDON_VERSION caught up after several missed bumps** ŌĆö first real allowlist add via the new report flow (v1.2.171). User reported a Reolink Duo 3 WiFi from their controls page; report landed in rweisbein/device-requests as issue #4 with the binary_sensors `_motion`, `_person`, `_vehicle`, `_animal` (motion device_class on the first, blank on the others ŌĆö typical Reolink). Added an entry to `CAMERA_MODELS` (`switches.py:687`) keyed by manufacturer "reolink" + model "Reolink Duo 3 WiFi" with those four trigger patterns; `detect_control_type` already handles partial manufacturer match + exact model match (case-insensitive both sides), so any Reolink Duo 3 WiFi will now appear on the controls page as a first-class camera with friendly name and the four trigger patterns auto-populated for trigger_entities matching. **Three companion fixes shipped in the same commit because the report itself surfaced them:**\n\n  (1) **`Addon Version: unknown` in the report body** ŌĆö `_get_addon_version()` (`webserver.py:48`) tried to read `version:` from `/app/config.yaml`, but the Dockerfile only copies `*.py *.html *.js *.png requirements.txt` (line 18) ŌĆö config.yaml never makes it into the running container. The function silently returned "unknown" every time. Fix: Dockerfile now sets `ENV ADDON_VERSION=${ADDON_VERSION}` from the existing build ARG (`Dockerfile:17`); `_get_addon_version()` reads `os.environ["ADDON_VERSION"]` first and falls back to config.yaml only for local dev runs. The build ARG was already declared (originally for cache-busting per the comment on line 15), so this is a one-line ENV addition + a few lines in the Python helper ŌĆö no plumbing to add.\n\n  (2) **Report payload only sent `model`** ŌĆö was `device.get("model_id") or device.get("model")` (single field, falling back through), so we couldn't tell from the issue body whether a manufacturer was reporting model_id or model_name. Reolink's Duo 3 WiFi reported only `model` (no model_id), but other manufacturers (Hue, IKEA) reliably populate both ŌĆö and they can differ across firmware versions, which means an allowlist key based on the friendly model name might miss a different firmware that reports model_id instead. Fix: payload now sends both fields explicitly (`model` and `model_id` as separate JSON keys); the issue body shows both, and we can pick the more stable one for the allowlist key per device family. Worker-side display code unchanged for now (still just renders `model`) ŌĆö separate worker redeploy with markdown for both fields would be a small follow-up.\n\n  (3) **build.yaml ADDON_VERSION drift** ŌĆö was still pinned at "1.2.167" since the v1.2.167 release; v1.2.168 through v1.2.171 all shipped with the build arg out of sync. Per the comment on Dockerfile line 15, ADDON_VERSION is a cache-buster (forces Docker to invalidate the COPY layer when the value changes), so missing the bumps meant Docker could in principle have served stale cached layers. In practice the COPY-layer hash includes file content so cache-busting via ARG is belt-and-suspenders, but with the new ENV ADDON_VERSION dependency we now actively need the build arg to match config.yaml ŌĆö otherwise the env var inside the container would lag the displayed version. Caught build.yaml up to 1.2.172 and we'll bump both files together going forward (the ship-it checklist already covered both, but the lapses confirm it's worth a one-time process audit on next ship).\n\n  Net effect for users: any Reolink Duo 3 WiFi in HA now shows up as "Reolink Duo 3 WiFi" on the controls page with the four trigger patterns pre-selected (no manual sensor-picking required); future device reports include accurate addon_version and both model fields so we have what we need to curate without follow-up; build pipeline now actually wires ADDON_VERSION into the running container instead of just naming a cache-key.

## 1.2.171
- **"Report" button on every device row in the Add control modal ŌĆö one-click submission to homeglo for unsupported-device curation** ŌĆö first half of the external-registry vision (project_camera_triggers.md). Today, devices not in the allowlist (CAMERA_MODELS/MOTION_SENSOR_MODELS/CONTACT_SENSOR_MODELS in switches.py) require us to manually curate each manufacturer/model and ship a new addon version. Users can still add them via the manual flow (search ŌåÆ pick ŌåÆ assign triggers), but we have no signal about which devices are in the field, so we can't prioritize what to allowlist next. This change adds the feedback channel: every device card in the Add control modal now has a small "Report" button (top-right, opacity 0.5 default ŌåÆ 1.0 on hover so it doesn't compete with the device-pick affordance, click stops propagation so it doesn't also fire `selectDevice`). Click sends manufacturer + model + integration + sw_version + addon_version + full binary_sensors list (entity_id + device_class for each) to a Cloudflare Worker at `homeglo-device-reports.rweisbein.workers.dev`, which files it as a GitHub issue in `rweisbein/device-requests` (private repo) using a fine-grained PAT scoped to issues:write on that one repo. Backend implementation: new `HOMEGLO_REPORT_WEBHOOK_URL` constant near top of webserver.py + `_get_addon_version()` helper that reads `version:` from config.yaml lazily and caches it (avoids three-place version bumps ŌĆö config.yaml stays the single source of truth) + new `report_device` endpoint at `/api/devices/report` that pulls the device from `client.device_registry`, walks `client.entity_registry` to collect all binary_sensor entities for that device_id with their `device_class`, builds the JSON payload, and POSTs to the webhook with a 10s timeout + structured error responses (502 for webhook errors, 504 for timeout, 503 if WS client not connected). Frontend: `reportDevice(deviceId, btn)` JS function with optimistic button state ("Sending..." ŌåÆ "Thanks!" or "Failed", reverts after 2.5s); CSS rules for `.acp-report-btn` (small, muted, hover-fade in). The webhook itself is a 70-line CF Worker (deployed separately via Cloudflare dashboard) that validates payload shape, builds a markdown issue body with manufacturer/model/integration/sw_version/addon_version + bulleted binary_sensors list with device_class, and POSTs to `api.github.com/repos/rweisbein/device-requests/issues` with a `device-request` label. CORS headers permissive (Allow-Origin: *) so the addon iframe can POST cross-origin. End-to-end verified: console fetch from example.com to the worker URL filed issue #1 in the device-requests repo successfully. Net effect: a user opens Add control, sees their device in the list, clicks "Report" ŌĆö within seconds, an issue lands in our triage queue with everything we need to add an allowlist entry. No GitHub account required from the user, no JSON to copy-paste, no email follow-up. Manual-add flow unchanged ŌĆö Report is purely a signal channel, not a substitute for adding the device. Future: extend Report button placement to the controls list itself (for inactive/legacy entries that didn't make it into the allowlist), and replace the bundled allowlist with a homeglo-hosted models.json that the addon fetches on startup, so new device support ships without an addon update.

## 1.2.170
- **Add control picker now hides already-configured switches and contact sensors (was: only motion sensors)** ŌĆö `search_devices` (`webserver.py:6438-6442`) built `configured_device_ids` from `get_all_motion_sensors()` only, so already-configured switches and contact sensors with a `binary_sensor.*` entity (rare but real for older Hue Dimmers like RWL020/021 that expose a `binary_sensor.*_button` companion in addition to ZHA events) leaked into the Add control modal as if they were unconfigured. Most switches don't have binary_sensors at all (they emit ZHA events instead, captured by main.py's event listener ŌĆö that's why most Hue Dimmers correctly stay out of the picker), but the older models that DO have a binary_sensor would appear duplicated. Same gap existed for contact sensors. Fix extends `configured_device_ids` to include `get_all_switches()` + `get_all_contact_sensors()` device_ids, so any already-configured control of any type now gets filtered out of the picker. Filter is by `device_id` ŌĆö same field auto-create populates and that the manual-add path now sets ŌĆö so the dedup is consistent across both creation paths. Net effect: picker only shows devices not yet known to the addon, regardless of category, matching the user's mental model of "show me things I can add."

## 1.2.169
- **Add control source: fix `__init__() got an unexpected keyword argument 'areas'` on submit** ŌĆö surfaced after v1.2.168 unblocked the modal: clicking Add with selected triggers errored 500. `add_control_source` (`webserver.py:6524`) constructed `MotionSensorConfig(areas=[], ...)`, but `MotionSensorConfig` was refactored from `areas: List[MotionAreaConfig]` to `scopes: List[MotionScope]` (`switches.py:1021`) ŌĆö `areas` is now only a derived `@property` that expands scopes for backward-compatible iteration, not a constructor field. The auto-create path at `webserver.py:5211` was migrated correctly during the scopes refactor (`scopes=[switches.MotionScope(areas=[area_id])]`), but the manual-add path was missed and the dataclass `__init__` rejected the `areas` keyword. Fix: switched `areas=[]` ŌåÆ `scopes=[]` so the manual-add path constructs an empty-scopes sensor (no areas assigned yet ŌĆö the user picks an area on the control detail page after the modal closes and navigates them there). Also added `inactive=True` for consistency with `_auto_create_controls` ŌĆö both auto-created and manually-added unconfigured controls now start paused until the user assigns a scope, which prevents a freshly-added trigger entity from firing actions in zero areas (no-op anyway, but defensively cleaner). Net effect: end-to-end manual add flow now works ŌĆö modal populates (v1.2.168), user picks device + triggers + clicks Add, sensor config persists, redirect to `./control/<device_id>` for area assignment.

## 1.2.168
- **Controls page Add control modal fixed: search uses relative URLs (was silently failing on `undefined` basePath)** ŌĆö `switches.html` referenced a `basePath` variable in five places (lines 1418, 1464, 1525, 1538, 1543) inside `searchDevices`/`selectDevice`/`addSelectedControl` and the post-add navigation, but `basePath` was never defined in that file or in `shared.js` ŌĆö only `control.html`, `area.html`, `moment.html`, and `rhythm-design.html` define it. The result: every modal fetch built a URL like `"undefined/api/devices/search?q="`, which either resolved to a wildcard-matched 404 path or threw a fetch error that was swallowed by an empty `catch (e) {}` at line 1422. The modal would open, render its "Searching..." placeholder, never populate, and never log anything ŌĆö devices with `binary_sensor.*` entities (Reolink cameras, etc.) were invisible despite the backend `/api/devices/search` endpoint working fine. The rest of the page (loadData, control configure, refresh) was unaffected because those fetches use relative URLs (`./api/controls`, `./api/areas`, `./api/config`, `./api/controls/{id}/configure`, `./api/controls/refresh`) ŌĆö only the modal block went through `basePath`. Fix: replace all five `basePath +` references with `./` relative paths matching the rest of the file. `fetch(basePath + '/api/devices/search?q=' + ...)` ŌåÆ `fetch('./api/devices/search?q=' + ...)`, same for the second `/api/devices/search` call in `selectDevice`, the POST to `/api/controls/add` in `addSelectedControl`, and the two `window.location.href = basePath + '/control/' + id` redirects after add success / already-configured cases. Relative paths resolve correctly through HA ingress because the addon is mounted at `/api/hassio_ingress/<token>/switches` and `./api/devices/search` resolves to `/api/hassio_ingress/<token>/api/devices/search` ŌĆö exactly the URL the addon's webserver is listening on. Verified the backend works by hitting `/api/devices/search` directly via the iframe context: returned 17 devices including the Reolink camera with its motion/person/vehicle binary_sensors visible. Net effect: clicking "+ Add control" on the controls page now actually populates the device picker, including non-allowlisted devices (Reolink, anything else with binary_sensors), so users can manually add cameras as motion-trigger sources without waiting for an allowlist update.

## 1.2.167
- **Area-details chart top reorganized: sun/moon/conditions chip moved ABOVE the 100% line, NOW pill brought down closer to plot top** ŌĆö visual fix for the overcrowded chart-top band introduced in v1.2.164/165. v1.2.164 had moved the sun/moon icons + conditions chip DOWN from the above-plot zone (paper y=1.05) to inside the plot top (paper y=0.97) to make room for the bigger NOW pill ŌĆö the trade was the icons started bleeding into the bulb curve at sunrise/sunset and the conditions chip overlapped the curve peak near noon. Net visual: sun and moon disc edges grazed the curve's leading/trailing flanks, "60% sun contribution" chip parked on top of the curve at midday, and the NOW pill sat way up in the chart-shell padding band with a noticeable gap between pill and plot top. User feedback: push sun/moon/chip up so they're cleanly above the 100% line, and bring NOW pill down so the whole top stack is more compact. Four coordinated changes. (1) **Plotly t margin bumped 36 ŌåÆ 50** (line 2751). Adds 14px of vertical room ABOVE the 100% line for sun/moon and chip to live in without competing with the curve. Plot area shrinks correspondingly (158px ŌåÆ 144px on the 280px-tall chartDiv) ŌĆö the bulb curves still have plenty of vertical room since both the wake and bed peaks rarely exceed ~80% of plot height. (2) **Sun/moon images repositioned from inside-plot to above-plot.** Previously: `y: 0.97, yanchor: 'top'` ŌåÆ image's TOP edge anchored at paper y=0.97 (top of plot area), spanning paper y=0.81 to 0.97 (i.e. inside the plot near the top). Now: `y: 1.04, yanchor: 'bottom'` ŌåÆ image's BOTTOM edge anchored at paper y=1.04 (just above the 100% line), spanning paper y=1.04 to 1.20 (entirely in Plotly's t-margin band, ABOVE the 100% line). `sizey: 0.16` preserved ŌĆö image height = 0.16 ├Ś 144px = 23px on the new plot, similar visual weight to v1.2.165's 25px on the older 158px plot. yanchor=bottom flip is the cleaner way to express "sit above the plot top" because anchoring at the bottom edge of the image at y=1.04 tells the renderer the image's baseline is just above 100%, rather than computing top-anchor + height inversely. Applied identically to both sunrise (line ~2625) and sunset (line ~2652) image entries. The transparent hover-helper scatter traces at `y: [100]` (line ~2633, ~2660) are unchanged ŌĆö they cover the icon's hit zone at the 100% gridline level which still reads correctly even with the icon now above the line, since hover hit on the visible icon disc still triggers within the scatter marker's tolerance. (3) **Conditions chip py formula flipped from BELOW 100% to ABOVE 100%.** Old formula at `updateChartSunInfo` (line ~4166): `py = chartTopInShell + fl.yaxis._offset + 0.07 * fl.yaxis._length - el.offsetHeight / 2` ŌĆö `+ 0.07` put the chip 7% of plot height BELOW the 100% line (inside plot, near the curve peak band, paper y Ōēł 0.93). New formula: `- 0.10 * fl.yaxis._length` ŌĆö chip now sits 10% of plot height ABOVE the 100% line (paper y Ōēł 1.10), in the same t-margin band as the sun/moon icons. Since chip is centered at solar noon x and sun/moon are at sunrise/sunset x, no horizontal overlap; vertical alignment in the same band reads as a coherent "sunrise / weather chip / sunset" row stretched across the day from morning to evening. Comment updated to reflect new placement. (4) **`#chart-shell` padding-top reduced 32 ŌåÆ 16** (line 532). NOW pill is `position: absolute` at `top: 4px` of chart-shell, so reducing padding doesn't move the pill itself ŌĆö it moves chartDiv UP by 16px, which closes the gap between pill bottom and plot top. New geometry: chart-shell-top ŌåÆ 4px (NOW pill top) ŌåÆ ~28px (NOW pill bottom) ŌåÆ 16px (chart-shell padding-top boundary, where chartDiv begins) ŌåÆ 50px (Plotly t margin band, hosting sun/moon/chip) ŌåÆ 66px (100% line) ŌåÆ ... rest of plot. Net effect: NOW pill bottom sits slightly BELOW chartDiv top, overlapping the first ~12px of Plotly's t margin (which is empty space anyway, no plot data lives there), with sun/moon/chip occupying the next ~38px of t margin. The cursor dashed line `y1: 1.24` (line ~2691) reaches paper y=1.24, which is 0.24 ├Ś 144 = 35px above the 100% line = chart-shell-top + 31px ŌĆö meets the NOW pill bottom (28px) within 3px, preserving the lineŌåÆpill connection visual. Other downstream elements considered: `_chartGeom.xAnchor` math, `updateChartHero` positioning (uses `chartDiv._fullLayout.xaxis._offset`), `updateChartNowPill` positioning (uses `chartDiv.getBoundingClientRect()`), Plotly mute overlay shape `y1: 0.88` ŌĆö all read DOM/Plotly state at runtime so they auto-adapt to the new t margin and padding without code changes. Top-of-plot stack now reads cleanly: NOW pill (cursor info) ŌåÆ sunrise icon / weather chip / sunset icon (solar context, all above the 100% line as a single horizontal band) ŌåÆ 100% line ŌåÆ bulb curves. No more icons bleeding into curves, no more chip overlapping curve peaks, NOW pill sits compact against the plot edge with the cursor line cleanly bridging to it.

## 1.2.166
- **Area-details Adjust card live-readout + ghost thumb, Auto-card Fade row restructured to value-left + slider-below** ŌĆö three coordinated UI fixes on area.html. (1) **Bright/Color hero readouts now update in real-time as the user drags.** Previously `previewSlider()` (line ~3495) updated the thumb position, track gradient, and chart curve on every pointermove, but the `#slider-hero-brightness` ("78%") and `#slider-hero-color` ("2910K") readouts above the tracks stayed frozen at their pre-drag values until pointerup triggered a state refresh from the server. The eye expects the displayed value to track the thumb continuously ŌĆö without it the slider felt disconnected from the readout. Added two `textContent` writes inside the brightness/color branches of `previewSlider`, immediately after `applyOneSlider`: brightness branch writes `Math.round(previewBri) + '%'`, color branch writes `Math.round(previewCCT) + 'K'`. Values match the bulb-space mapping the thumb position represents (`previewBri = bMin + (bMax-bMin) * position/100`), so the displayed number tracks the thumb x-position cleanly. After release the existing render path at line ~2918 takes over and re-derives the readout from `actual_brightness`/`effectiveCCT` ŌĆö the handoff is seamless because both paths converge on the override value the user just set. (2) **Ghost thumb during drag, mirroring the home page (areas.html) row-slider-thumb-ghost pattern.** New `.slider-thumb-ghost` div added to both Bright and Color `.slider-track` containers as a sibling of `.slider-thumb`. CSS: 18├Ś18 round (matching the live thumb dimensions at line 432-444), `background: transparent`, `border: 1.5px solid rgba(255,255,255,0.55)`, `display: none` by default, `display: block` when `.slider-track.dragging`. JS: in `initSliderHandlers`'s `onDown` handler, before the dragging class is applied, capture the current thumb left % via `parseFloat(thumb.style.left)` and write it to `ghost.style.left` ŌĆö anchors the ghost at the pre-drag position for the lifetime of the drag. Also inherits the live thumb's `borderColor` so the ghost reads as a faint duplicate of the same control rather than a generic ring. CSS `.slider-track.dragging .slider-thumb-ghost` reveal handles show/hide entirely off the existing `.dragging` class ŌĆö no extra teardown needed in `onUp`. Skipped the `.row-slider-fill-drag` band (the faint connector areas.html stretches between ghost and live thumb to encode delta direction) ŌĆö only the ghost was requested. (3) **Auto On/Off Fade rows restructured: value left-aligned in content column, slider on a row below that reveals on tap.** Previous layout had the slider + value on a single row inside `.auto-sched-field-content` with `justify-content: flex-end`, and the slider's reveal was a same-row width=0 collapse: tap the row ŌåÆ slider expanded from `flex: 0 0 0; opacity: 0` to `flex: 1 1 auto; opacity: 1` while the "5 min" value sat right-edge of the content column. Two visual problems: (a) the value's right-anchor didn't match Time/Light/If rows (where content starts at the left edge of the content column), so Fade looked like a different kind of field; (b) the same-row collapse made the row visually shrink on tap rather than expand below, breaking the convention rhythm-design.html's night-warming/sun-cooling Start/End/Fade reveal-groups establish elsewhere in the project. New layout: `.auto-sched-field-content` now contains the `.auto-sched-fade-val` first (so the value sits at the start of the content column, left-aligned with how Time's day buttons / Light's pills / If's checkbox start theirs), followed by a `.auto-fade-slider-row` div containing the `<input type=range>`. CSS: `.auto-fade-row .auto-fade-slider-row { max-height: 0; opacity: 0; overflow: hidden }` collapses the slider row by default; `.auto-fade-row.is-revealing .auto-fade-slider-row { max-height: 32px; opacity: 1; margin-top: 6px }` reveals it on tap. The `.reveal-group` class was already in place (since v1.2.156) and `initAutoHideSliders()` (line ~3639) already handles tap-to-toggle plus the range-input click guard, so the click affordance works for free with the new structure. Dropped the now-unused `.auto-fade-row .auto-sched-field-content { justify-content: flex-end }` and the same-row width-collapse rules. Old slider styling (`flex: 1` on the slider, `min-width: 3.5em; text-align: right` on the value) replaced by `width: 100%` slider + value with no min-width/right-align. Both the auto-on Fade row (line ~1365) and auto-off Fade row (line ~1452) updated identically. Net effect: Fade now reads as a peer of Time/Light/If ŌĆö `Fade  5 min` left-aligned in the row, and tapping anywhere in the row reveals the slider in a clean second row beneath. Also resolves a small consistency win ŌĆö the area-details Auto card's Fade interaction now matches the rhythm-design page's Start/End/Fade interaction model.

## 1.2.165
- **Area-details chart taller (220px ŌåÆ 280px) + sun/moon icons sized up (sizey 0.08 ŌåÆ 0.16)** ŌĆö v1.2.164 moved the sun/moon icons inside the plot top (paper y=0.97) and shrank them to sizey=0.08, but with the chart container fixed at 220px the resulting plot area was only ~98px tall (220 - Plotly t:36 - b:86), so 0.08 of paper height = ~8px icons. Visibly tiny in the rendered output, and the overall chart felt vertically compressed compared to v1.2.163 because the moved icons + conditions chip ate into the same vertical band the curve previously had to itself. Two-part fix. (1) `#mini-chart` height bumped 220px ŌåÆ 280px ŌĆö plot area grows to ~158px, giving the bulb curve more vertical room and de-compressing the visual. (2) Sun + moon `sizey` bumped 0.08 ŌåÆ 0.16, doubling the paper-height ratio so icons render at ~25px on the new taller plot (vs ~13px on a sized-up plot at 0.08, or ~16px on the old 220px plot at 0.10). Result: sunrise / weather chip / sunset row in the plot top reads clearly with proportional icon sizes, NOW pill above the plot still has its own dedicated headroom, and the bulb curve has more vertical space to express its peak/trough shape. The mute overlay y1=0.88 still spares the moon (which now spans paper y=0.81-0.97 instead of 0.89-0.97 ŌĆö still above the y=0.88 mute boundary at the top edge but its bottom edge dips below; minor cosmetic that won't be visible since moon SVG is mostly transparent at its outer disc edges where the mute would render). Other downstream effects considered: `chart-shell` sticky region grows ~60px taller (32px padding-top from v1.2.164 + 60px more chart height), pushing subsequent content (Adjust card, Controls list, Auto card) down by that amount. Acceptable since chart is the focal element and was visibly cramped.

## 1.2.164
- **Area-details NOW pill becomes an HTML overlay (rounded corners + crisp font), sun/moon + conditions chip relocate to a horizontal band inside plot top, "NOW" prefix dropped in real-time, NOW dot border matches bed/wake** ŌĆö five-part follow-up after v1.2.163 review revealed several issues with the NOW-pill polish pass. (1) **Pill replaced with HTML overlay** ŌĆö v1.2.163 added `borderradius: 8` to the Plotly annotation, but Plotly annotations don't actually support `borderradius` (only shape rects support `cornerradius`); the property was silently ignored and the pill rendered with square corners. Replaced the annotation entirely with `<div id="chart-now-pill" class="chart-now-pill">` inside `#chart-shell`, positioned via JS at the cursor's x-pixel after each Plotly render. New `updateChartNowPill()` function mirrors the existing `updateChartHero` positioning math: reads `chartDiv._fullLayout.xaxis._offset` + `_length`, computes the cursor's pixel position relative to chart-shell, sets `pill.style.left = px + 'px'` (with translateX(-50%) on the pill so the text centers on the cursor). Pill text/color/bg/border are stashed on `_chartNowPillData` by `renderMiniChart` and consumed by `updateChartNowPill` after `Plotly.react` resolves. CSS gives genuine rounded corners (`border-radius: 8px`), crisp 13px / weight 600 font, 1.5px solid border, 3px 10px padding ŌĆö visually matching rhythm-design's `.ct-cursor-pill` styling. Also fixes a tertiary issue: Plotly annotation text was rendered as SVG <text> with default font weight; HTML span pill picks up the page's font-smoothing + weight rendering for cleaner glyphs. (2) **"NOW" prefix dropped in real-time mode** ŌĆö text was `NOW   5:17p ┬Ę 35% ┬Ę 5100K`, but in live mode the time IS now (cursor is at currentHour by definition), so the prefix added no information beyond what the time value carried. Dropped to `5:17p ┬Ę 35% ┬Ę 5100K`. "FROZEN" prefix preserved when `state.frozen_at != null` since in that case the time refers to the freeze moment, not the actual now ŌĆö the prefix carries real disambiguation there. (3) **Sun + moon SVG markers moved DOWN inside plot top, conditions chip moved to solar noon** ŌĆö v1.2.163 left sun/moon at paper y=1.05 (above the plot, in Plotly's t margin), while the bigger NOW pill at y=1.32 sat just above. With pill widening due to larger font, cursor positions near sunrise/sunset would push the pill into the sun/moon icons (~150px clearance at typical cursor positions, eaten up by the ~25% wider pill). Cleaner solution: separate the bands. Sun/moon now at paper y=0.97 with sizey=0.08 (down from 0.10) ŌĆö they sit just inside the top of the plot, spanning paper y=0.89-0.97. Conditions chip (`#chart-sun-info`) was statically positioned `top: 8px; right: 12px` in chart-shell; `updateChartSunInfo` now computes solar noon as `(sunrise + sunset) / 2`, converts to pixel via `_fullLayout.xaxis._offset + ((noon - xAnchor) / 24) * fl.xaxis._length`, and sets `el.style.left = (px - el.offsetWidth/2) + 'px'`, `el.style.top = (chartTop + yOffset + 0.07 * yLength - el.offsetHeight/2) + 'px'`, `el.style.right = 'auto'` to override the static CSS. Result: sunrise / weather / sunset render in a single horizontal band INSIDE the plot top, with sun at sunrise x, weather at solar noon x, moon at sunset x ŌĆö natural solar-day visual ordering. The above-plot zone is now reserved exclusively for the NOW pill. Mute overlay y1=0.88 still spares the moon (which now spans 0.89-0.97 instead of 0.91-1.05) ŌĆö clearance preserved. (4) **`#chart-shell` padding-top bumped 4px ŌåÆ 32px** to make dedicated room for the HTML NOW pill above the plot. ChartDiv now starts 32px below chart-shell top; pill at top:4px lives in that padding band, ~24px tall, with a small gap before chartDiv. Plotly's t:36 internal margin still leaves room for axis ticks at top; the cursor dashed line (paper y1=1.24) extends up through Plotly's t margin and clips at chartDiv top, ending just below the pill bottom ŌĆö line + pill read as connected. (5) **NOW dot border now black `#0a0a0a` (matching bed/wake handle)** ŌĆö was `'rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.7)'` (white-ish) when not frozen and `'rgba(99, 179, 237, 0.9)'` (blue) when frozen. The white/blue border read as a different kind of marker than the bed/wake handle's solid black border, breaking the dual-focus visual symmetry from v1.2.163. Both anchor markers (NOW dot + active phase handle) now use identical 2px black outline ŌĆö they read as twin focal points, both "this is a place that matters." Frozen state still distinguishes via fill color (light blue `rgba(120, 190, 240, 0.95)`) and pill prefix ("FROZEN"); the marker outline doesn't need to additionally change. Frozen pill bg/border alpha bumped 0.55 ŌåÆ 0.85 in same pass for parity with the new floor on the regular tinted-pill path.

## 1.2.163
- **Home page area cards: next-auto pill drops the relative time hint unless the fire is within 2h** ŌĆö small visual de-noise pass on the area-card auto-schedule pills. Each area card on the home page renders an "On" / "Off" next-auto pill via `formatAutoSchedulePill` (areas.html line 1568) that combines an arrow (`Ō¢▓`/`Ō¢╝`), the absolute time or sun-relative label (e.g. `Sunset +1h`, `7:30p`, `9p Mon`), and a trailing relative-hint span like `┬Ę 22m` or `┬Ę 7h` showing how long until the schedule fires. The hint was useful when the fire is *imminent* (you're about to be auto-dimmed in 22 minutes ŌĆö good to know) but added clutter for far-out fires (`Ō¢╝ Sunset ┬Ę 7h` doesn't tell you anything `Ō¢╝ Sunset` alone didn't already convey, and the `┬Ę 7h` reads as a third independent piece of info competing with the time and arrow for attention). The whole point of the pill is "next thing that's going to happen" ŌĆö at 7h out, the user isn't actually going to act on that information; at 22m out, they might. Gated the relative hint to only render when `diffH > 0 && diffH <= 2` (within 2 hours). Computed inline in `formatAutoSchedulePill` using the same `fireOff * 24 + decimal_hour - nowH` formula `formatRelativeFromFire` itself uses internally, so the gate matches the function's own time math exactly (no risk of the gate saying "show" when the function returns empty, or vice versa). Outside the 2h window the pill renders cleanly as `Ō¢▓ 6:30a` / `Ō¢╝ Sunset +1h` / `Ō¢▓ 7p Mon` ŌĆö arrow + time only. Inside the 2h window the trailing `┬Ę 22m` / `┬Ę 1h 30m` reappears, drawing the eye to the imminent action. Paused schedules (where `t === 'paused'`) and schedules missing `decimal_hour` data continue to suppress the hint as before. Other guards preserved: `t && t !== 'paused'` (no hint for paused schedules), `decimal_hour != null` (no hint without timing data). 2h threshold chosen as the rough upper bound where "minutes" naming kicks in (under 1h is `Nm`, 1-2h is `Nh` or `1h Nm` ŌĆö both still useful at-a-glance; 3h+ is essentially "later today" which the absolute time already conveys cleanly). Single-call-site change in areas.html lines 1595-1607.
- **Area-details chart: dual-focus on NOW + bed/wake handle, NOW pill typography upgrade, brightness-tint readability floor** ŌĆö five-part polish pass on the Adjust chart's anchor markers and pill, plus a global tinting floor that propagates to area-details header and home page area cards. (1) **NOW dot bumped to size 16, matching the bed/wake active handle.** Previously the on-curve NOW dot was size 9 (with an underlying size-8 cyan hover-helper at the same x,y). The bed/wake handle marker (the draggable "shift wake" / "shift bed" dot at `(activeMidHour, handleY)`) is size 16.
